###begin article-title 0
###xml 65 70 65 70 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trans</italic>
###xml 133 134 133 134 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn1">*</xref>
Calmodulin Association with Connexin32-derived Peptides Suggests trans-Domain Interaction in Chemical Gating of Gap Junction Channels*
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 163 181 163 181 <email xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k.torok@sgul.ac.uk</email>
 To whom correspondence should be addressed: BMS, SGUL, Cranmer Terrace, London, SW17 0RE United Kingdom. Tel.: 44-20-87-25-58-32; Fax: 44-20-87-25-35-81; E-mail: k.torok@sgul.ac.uk. 
###end p 1
###begin p 2
###xml 0 15 0 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Author's Choice</italic>
Author's Choice
###end p 2
###begin p 3
 applies to Author Choice Articles
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 484 486 484 486 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 723 725 723 725 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 754 755 754 755 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 755 758 755 758 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3,4</sub>
###xml 773 775 771 773 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 797 798 795 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 798 801 796 799 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1,2</sub>
###xml 817 819 813 815 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 991 992 987 988 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 992 995 988 991 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3,4</sub>
###xml 1010 1012 1004 1006 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 1016 1017 1010 1011 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 1017 1018 1011 1012 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 1034 1036 1026 1028 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 1041 1042 1033 1034 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 1042 1043 1034 1035 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 1051 1053 1043 1045 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 1312 1317 1304 1309 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trans</italic>
###xml 1328 1333 1320 1325 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trans</italic>
Calmodulin plays a key role in the chemical gating of gap junction channels. Two calmodulin-binding regions have previously been identified in connexin32 gap junction protein, one in the N-terminal and another in the C-terminal cytoplasmic tail of the molecule. The aim of this study was to better understand how calmodulin interacts with the connexin32-binding domains. Lobe-specific interactions of calmodulin with connexin32 peptides were studied by stopped flow kinetics, using Ca2+ binding-deficient mutants. Peptides corresponding to the N-terminal tail (residues 1-22) of connexin32 engaged both the N- and C-terminal lobes (N- and C-lobes) of calmodulin, binding with higher affinity to the C-lobe of calmodulin (Ca2+ dissociation rate constants k3,4, 1.7 +/- 0.5 s-1) than to the N-lobe (k1,2, 10.8 +/- 1.3 s-1). In contrast, peptides representing the C-terminal tail domain (residues 208-227) of connexin32 bound either the C- or the N-lobe but only one calmodulin lobe at a time (k3,4, 2.6 +/- 0.1 s-1 or k1, 13.8 +/- 0.5 s-1 and k2, 1000 s-1). The calmodulin-binding domains of the N- and C-terminal tails of connexin32 were best defined as residues 1-21 and 216-227, respectively. Our data, showing separate functions of the N- and C-lobes of calmodulin in the interactions with connexin32, suggest trans-domain or trans-subunit bridging by calmodulin as a possible mechanism of gap junction gating.
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 0 15 0 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Author's Choice</italic>

###end p 6
###begin p 7
###xml 241 242 241 242 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="fn" rid="fn2">2</xref>
###xml 244 245 244 245 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref1">1</xref>
###xml 434 440 434 440 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1</xref>
Gap junctions mediate direct intercellular communication by allowing the passage of ions and soluble molecules between cells. Gap junction channels are composed of two hemichannels (connexons); each connexon is composed of six connexins (Cx)2 (1). Each Cx polypeptide chain contains an N-terminal tail, four transmembrane domains (M1, M2, M3, and M4), two extracellular loops (EL1 and EL2), a cytoplasmic loop, and a C-terminal tail (Fig. 1).
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 60 61 60 61 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 61 62 61 62 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">j</sub>
###xml 67 69 67 69 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 76 77 76 77 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">+</sup>
###xml 79 80 79 80 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref2">2</xref>
###xml 81 82 81 82 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref5">5</xref>
###xml 85 86 85 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 86 87 86 87 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">j</sub>
###xml 151 152 151 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 152 153 152 153 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">j</sub>
###xml 308 309 308 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 373 374 373 374 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 374 375 374 375 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">j</sub>
###xml 450 451 450 451 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 451 452 451 452 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">j</sub>
###xml 469 470 469 470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref6">6</xref>
###xml 546 547 546 547 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 547 548 547 548 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">j</sub>
###xml 629 630 629 630 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">V</italic>
###xml 630 631 630 631 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">j</sub>
Gap junction channels are gated by transjunctional voltage (Vj), Ca2+, and H+ (2-5). Vj gradients activate two types of gates: fast and slow. The fast Vj gate flickers rapidly between the open and residual states, whereas the chemical/slow gate undergoes slow transitions between the open and closed states (6). Cytosolic acidification of small cells subjected to moderate Vj gradients allows the chemical/slow gate to be distinguished from the fast Vj-sensitive gate (6). Uncouplers activate a chemical gate that behaves identically to the slow Vj gate in terms of kinetics and efficiency. Thus, although chemical gate and slow Vj gate are usually referred to as separate gates, they may have closely related or identical mechanisms.
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 2 4 2 4 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 10 11 10 11 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">+</sup>
###xml 170 171 170 171 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref7">7</xref>
###xml 208 210 208 210 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 229 231 229 231 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 232 233 232 233 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">i</sub>
###xml 232 233 232 233 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><sub>i</sub></italic>
###xml 264 265 264 265 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 302 303 302 303 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref8">8</xref>
###xml 322 324 322 324 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 325 326 325 326 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">i</sub>
###xml 325 326 325 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><sub>i</sub></italic>
###xml 429 430 429 430 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref5">5</xref>
###xml 513 515 513 515 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 516 517 516 517 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">i</sub>
###xml 516 517 516 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><sub>i</sub></italic>
###xml 543 545 543 545 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
Ca2+ and H+ are pivotal to the operation of gap junctions because their concentrations within the cell dictate whether the junction is opened or closed (reviewed in Ref. 7). Increases in intracellular free Ca2+ concentration ([Ca2+]i) in the range of 200 to 1000 nm induce the opening of hemichannels (8). In contrast, [Ca2+]i in the high nanomolar to low micromolar range inhibits gap junctional communication (reviewed in Ref. 5), indicating that gap junction channels and hemichannels are both sensitive to [Ca2+]i but may be affected by Ca2+ in opposite ways.
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 76 78 76 78 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 142 144 142 144 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 207 208 207 208 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref5">5</xref>
###xml 210 211 210 211 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref9">9</xref>
###xml 212 214 212 214 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 239 241 239 241 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 389 391 389 391 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 406 408 406 408 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 495 497 495 497 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref13">13</xref>
###xml 506 508 506 508 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 884 886 880 882 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref14">14</xref>
###xml 914 916 910 912 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 982 984 978 980 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1138 1140 1134 1136 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 1271 1273 1267 1269 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1275 1277 1271 1273 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 1330 1332 1326 1328 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1419 1421 1415 1417 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1435 1437 1431 1433 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref15">15</xref>
###xml 1662 1664 1654 1656 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>
###xml 1730 1732 1722 1724 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1897 1899 1889 1891 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 2042 2044 2034 2036 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 2056 2058 2048 2050 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 2174 2176 2166 2168 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 2265 2267 2257 2259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 2306 2308 2298 2300 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref18">18</xref>
The molecular mechanisms of gap junction gating are still poorly defined. Ca2+ may act via calmodulin (CaM) inducing an interaction between Ca2+-bound CaM and one or more intracellular domains of connexins (5, 9-12). CaM is a ubiquitous Ca2+-binding protein of 16.8 kDa (148 amino acids) with a sequence that is well conserved from plants to mammals. CaM has a high affinity for binding Ca2+, and in its Ca2+ bound form, CaM binds to a large number of target proteins regulating their function (13). The Ca2+-binding sites of CaM comprise four helix-loop-helix EF hands situated in two globular lobes; EF hands 1 and 2 are located in the N-terminal lobe (N-lobe), and EF hands 3 and 4 are found in the highly homologous C-terminal lobe (C-lobe). The N- and C-lobes are separated by a 30-amino acid linker, which, although appearing alpha-helical in crystals, is flexible in solution (14). The C-terminal lobe of Ca2+-free (apo) CaM has an about 5-fold higher affinity for binding Ca2+ because of the semi-open conformation of its two EF hands, differing significantly from the fully closed conformation of EF hands 1 and 2 in the N-lobe (15). This semi-open conformation adopted by the C-terminal lobe accounts for the ability of CaM to bind peptides in the absence of Ca2+ (15). Many target peptides, however, bind to CaM in a Ca2+-dependent manner, associating with the more open hydrophobic pockets exposed in the Ca2+-bound state (15). The bound peptide, once subjected to the hydrophobic pockets, tends to form an alpha-helical structure, often flanked by a Trp residue near the N terminus and a Phe, or other bulky hydrophobic residues, at the C terminus (16). CaM undergoes a number of structural changes upon binding of Ca2+. We have shown by Forster resonance energy transfer that apo-CaM exists in an extended conformation, with maximum distance between the N- and C-lobes, whereas in Ca2+.CaM.peptide complexes, the conformation of CaM is more compact as indicated by the significantly reduced distance between its N- and C-lobes (17). In the Ca2+-bound state (holo-CaM), CaM exists in a dynamic equilibrium of two major conformations, extended and semi-compact (17). This allows it enough flexibility to bind targets in variably extended conformations (17) and to form interdomain connections (18).
###end p 10
###begin p 11

###end p 11
###begin p 12
###xml 0 144 0 144 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Schematic diagram of a Cx32 polypeptide chain spanning the membrane, data for residue numbers and positions obtained from NCBI data base search.</bold>
###xml 272 274 272 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CL</italic>

The figure shows the N-terminal tail (residues 1-22), four transmembrane domains (M1, M2, M3, and M4), the intracellular loop (CL, residues 96-130), and the C-terminal tail (residues 215-283).
###end p 12
###begin p 13
###xml 112 113 112 113 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref9">9</xref>
###xml 115 117 115 117 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref10">10</xref>
###xml 397 399 397 399 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 580 581 580 581 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 579 581 579 581 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 587 588 587 588 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 601 603 601 603 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 622 624 622 624 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 719 720 719 720 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 718 720 718 720 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 730 731 729 730 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 745 747 744 746 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 766 768 765 767 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 957 963 956 962 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig1" ref-type="fig">Fig. 1</xref>
###xml 1180 1182 1179 1181 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref19">19</xref>
###xml 1183 1185 1182 1184 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref22">22</xref>
The possibility that CaM is involved in gap junction regulation was first proposed by Peracchia and co-workers (9, 10), suggesting a CaM-binding site at the C-terminal tail of connexin32 (Cx32, Gjb1). Previously, we have identified, by equilibrium binding studies, two CaM-binding domains in Cx32, a novel site in the N-terminal tail, and a site in the previously proposed C-terminal tail region (12). The peptide, consisting of residues 1-21, which represents the N-terminal tail CaM-binding domain of Cx32, bound to the fluorescent CaM derivative, TA-CaM with a high affinity (Kd, 27 nm) and in a Ca2+-dependent manner (12). The peptide representing residues 216-230 of the Cx32 C-terminal tail, bound TA-CaM with a Kd of 2.1 mum, also in a Ca2+-dependent manner (12). Interestingly, both the N-terminal and the C-terminal tail CaM-binding domains of Cx32 are located close to the membrane and are contiguous with hydrophobic membrane-spanning sequences (Fig. 1). Furthermore, although the C-terminal tail CaM-binding domain in Cx32 represents only 15% of the C-terminal tail of Cx32, the removal of the other 85% had little effect on junction permeability and chemical gating (19-22).
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 102 104 102 104 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref23">23</xref>
###xml 152 154 152 154 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref24">24</xref>
###xml 253 255 253 255 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref19">19</xref>
###xml 257 259 257 259 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref20">20</xref>
###xml 482 484 482 484 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 510 512 510 512 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref23">23</xref>
Recently, CaM has also been shown to bind peptides matching a cytoplasmic loop domain of Cx43 (Gja1) (23) and C-terminal tail domains of Cx36 and Cx35 (24), suggesting that CaM plays a role in the function of several connexins. Peracchia and coworkers (19, 20), using Cx chimera Cx32/38IL, have shown that a domain in the second half of the cytoplasmic loop may be involved in the chemical gating mechanism of Cx32. Because this region in Cx32 does not contain a CaM-binding motif (12), in contrast with Cx43 (23), the mechanism of this involvement is yet to be determined.
###end p 14
###begin p 15
###xml 199 201 199 201 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 221 223 221 223 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 539 541 539 541 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 571 572 571 572 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 572 575 572 575 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
Here, we explore the binding of CaM to Cx32 domains to better understand how CaM participates in the chemical gating mechanism of gap junction channels. To assess the binding potential of all four Ca2+ sites of CaM two Ca2+ binding-deficient CaM mutants were used: CaM12, in which a single-point mutation was made in each of the two N-lobe EF hands, and CaM34, in which single-point mutation was applied to each of the two C-lobe EF hands of CaM. CaM mutants were combined with Cx32-derived peptides and using stopped flow kinetics; the Ca2+ dissociation rate constants (koff) were measured. In addition, a resonance energy transfer CaM derivative was used to explore CaM conformation in the Cx32 peptide complexes and helped establish a more exact definition of the two CaM-binding regions of Cx32.
###end p 15
###begin title 16
MATERIALS AND METHODS
###end title 16
###begin p 17
###xml 0 7 0 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Vectors</italic>
###xml 121 137 121 137 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 160 161 160 161 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">4</sub>
###xml 244 246 244 246 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 450 457 450 457 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. coli</italic>
###xml 8 13 <span type="species:ncbi:9606">Human</span>
###xml 121 137 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
###xml 450 457 <span type="species:ncbi:562">E. coli</span>
Vectors-Human liver wild type CaM was subcloned between restriction sites NdeI for the 5' and PstI for the 3' end in the Escherichia coli expression vector pAED4. CaM and the T34C/T110C double mutant CaM were generated as previously described (17). CaM12 (D22A/D58A CaM) and CaM34 (D95A/D131A CaM) cDNA-s, kindly provided by Dr. J. P. Adelman (Vollum Institute, Portland, OR), were subcloned in the BamHI (5') and EcoRI (3') restriction sites in the E. coli expression vector pET-21b by Dr. Nael Nadif Kasri (Katholic University of Leuven, Leuven, Belgium). DNA sequencing confirmed that the mutations were in the desired positions.
###end p 17
###begin p 18
###xml 0 35 0 35 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Protein Expression and Purification</italic>
###xml 127 129 127 129 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 278 280 278 280 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 391 393 391 393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
Protein Expression and Purification-Wild type and mutant CaM-s were expressed and purified by previously described procedures (17). Final purification to homogeneity was performed by HPLC and the purity, and identity of the proteins is confirmed by mass spectrometry as in Ref. 17. The concentrations of CaM, its mutants, and fluorescent derivatives were determined as previously described (17).
###end p 18

###begin p 21
###xml 0 15 0 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">CD Spectroscopy</italic>
###xml 227 228 227 228 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 286 287 286 287 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 673 674 663 664 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 674 676 664 666 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 679 681 669 671 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 777 779 767 769 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref33">33</xref>
CD Spectroscopy-CD spectra were collected using a Chirascan spectropolarimeter in the wavelength ranges of 185-260 and 230-400 nm. Protein samples were desalted, freeze-dried, and dissolved in phosphate-buffered saline and 10 mm EGTA. The instrument was flushed continuously with pure N2 gas throughout the experiment to improve performance below 200 nm. The path length was 0.5 mm for far UV and 1 mm for near UV measurements. All of the spectra were acquired at room temperature and were buffer base line-subtracted. The far UV CD spectra were corrected for concentration and path length and expressed in terms of molar differential extinction coefficient, Deltaepsilon (m-1 cm-1). Secondary structure estimation was calculated using the Principle Component Analysis method (33).
###end p 21
###begin p 22
###xml 0 6 0 6 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">DA-CaM</italic>
###xml 87 89 87 89 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 310 311 310 311 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">R</italic>
###xml 311 312 311 312 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">o</sub>
###xml 324 326 324 326 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 679 681 679 681 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 784 788 784 788 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">e.g.</italic>
###xml 833 835 829 831 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 867 869 863 865 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref25">25</xref>
###xml 895 897 891 893 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
DA-CaM-The synthesis, characterization, and properties of DA-CaM are described in Ref. 17. In short, cysteine residues in the double mutant T34C/T110C-CaM were labeled with the fluorophore, IAEDANS and DDP, a quencher compound. The two probes IAEDANS and DDP form a Forster resonance energy transfer pair with Ro of 2.6 nm (17); increased quenching of the donor AEDANS fluorescence by the acceptor DDP indicates close proximity of the probes and hence of the N- and C-CaM lobes. Following random labeling of the two sites, T34C and T110C, the labeled mixture was fractionated by HPLC to separate the CaM fractions labeled with different fluorophores at each lobe, termed DA-CaM (17). DA-CaM fractions were identified by maximum donor quenching displayed upon binding target peptides, e.g. CaM-binding domain peptides of alphaCaMKII (17) or myosin light chain kinase (25). These peptides cause Ca2+/CaM, which exists in an equilibrium of extended and semi-compact conformations to bind in a compact conformation.
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Peptides</italic>
###xml 174 176 174 176 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 432 433 426 427 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">o</sub>
###xml 442 443 436 437 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 443 445 437 439 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 448 450 442 444 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 605 606 599 600 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 711 712 699 700 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">o</sub>
###xml 721 722 709 710 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 722 724 710 712 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 727 729 715 717 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
Peptides-Cx32 (Gjb1) peptides were synthesized at the University of Rochester (Rochester, NY) and were purified to homogeneity by HPLC using previously described procedures (17). The concentrations of the two Cx32 N-terminal tail peptides representing residues 1-19 (MNWTGLYTLLSGVNRHSTA, mass 2121.4 Da) and 1-22 (MNWTGLYTLLSGVNRHSTAIGR, mass 2447.8 Da) were determined spectroscopically using a molar extinction coefficient epsilono of 7100 m-1 cm-1. The concentrations of the two Cx32 C-terminal tail peptides representing residues 208-226 and 208-227 (EVVYLIIRACARRAQRRSN and Ac-EVVYLIIRACARRAQRRSNP-NH2, masses 2274.7 and 2413.9 Da, respectively) were determined using a molar extinction coefficient epsilono of 1400 m-1 cm-1.
###end p 23
###begin p 24
###xml 0 12 0 12 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Fluorescence</italic>
###xml 178 179 178 179 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 181 182 181 182 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">+</sup>
###xml 203 204 203 204 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 213 214 213 214 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 219 220 219 220 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 227 228 226 227 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 270 272 269 271 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 292 293 290 291 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 331 332 328 329 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 335 337 332 334 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
Fluorescence excitation was set to 320 nm with 1-nm slit width and fluorescence emission from quin 2 was collected using a 530-nm cutoff filter. The assay solution contained 50 mm K+-PIPES, pH 7.0, 100 mm KCl, 2 mm MgCl2. 90 mum quin 2 in assay solution with no added Ca2+ was mixed with 3 mum CaM or CaM.peptide complexes in 50 mum Ca2+-containing buffer solution (mixing chamber concentrations). Care was taken that all of the protein components were free of EGTA.
###end p 24
###begin p 25
###xml 0 86 0 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Conformation Studies and Equilibrium Binding Measurements of Cx32 Peptides with DA-CaM</italic>
###xml 236 238 236 238 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 352 353 352 353 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 351 353 351 353 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
Conformation Studies and Equilibrium Binding Measurements of Cx32 Peptides with DA-CaM-Equilibrium fluorescence titrations of DA-CaM and Cx32 peptide binding were carried out using an ISS-SLM spectrofluorimeter as previously described (17) to assess the degree of compactness of CaM in Cx32 peptide complexes and to measure the dissociation constant (Kd) for CaM binding by Cx32 peptides.
###end p 25
###begin p 26
###xml 0 8 0 8 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Software</italic>
Software-Stopped flow kinetic data were fitted using the KinetAsyst software program (Hi-Tech Scientific). Equilibrium binding fluorescence data were analyzed using GraFit software program, version 4.0. CaM binding propensity prediction was obtained using software provided by the Department of Medical Biophysics, University of Toronto.
###end p 26
###begin p 27
###xml 0 20 0 20 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Statistical Analysis</italic>
###xml 160 161 160 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 163 164 163 164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">3</xref>
###xml 166 167 166 167 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 445 446 445 446 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 498 499 498 499 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">1</xref>
###xml 501 502 501 502 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">2</xref>
###xml 504 505 504 505 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl3">3</xref>
###xml 746 747 744 745 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 747 750 745 748 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
###xml 775 776 771 772 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
Statistical Analysis-For each data set the stopped flow kinetic experiments produced five to nine records; these records were averaged and can be seen in Figs. 2, 3, 4; for the averaged records an "S.D. fit" was determined that indicates the standard deviation of the data from the fit. From independent averages a mean was produced for each type of experiment; the number of independent averages included in the mean is displayed in the format n = number of experiments and can be found in Tables 1, 2, 3. The S.D. associated with all data under "Results" and in the tables is a measurement of the standard deviation of the mean from all the averages and is denoted by either S.D. or the +/- symbol. Typically, data are presented in the format: koff value +/- S.D. of mean (n = the number of independent experiments).
###end p 27
###begin p 28
###xml 0 7 0 7 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">TABLE 1</label>
###xml 9 11 9 11 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 7 56 7 56 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Ca<sup>2+</sup> dissociation kinetics of CaM and mutant CaMs</bold>
###xml 7 56 7 56 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" textid="29"><bold>Ca<sup>2+</sup> dissociation kinetics of CaM and mutant CaMs</bold></p>
###xml 94 95 94 95 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 95 98 95 98 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
###xml 204 205 204 205 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 312 313 312 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 422 424 422 424 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 434 435 434 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 639 641 639 641 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 56 689 56 689 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" textid="30">The mean dissociation rate constants (<italic>k</italic><sub>off</sub>) and the standard deviation are shown for each EF hand in wild type CaM, CaM12, and CaM34, respectively; <italic>n</italic> refers to the number of independent experiments from which the data was obtained. The relative amplitude (<italic>A</italic>) is also shown for each EF hand; this represents the involvement of the particular hand in the binding of Ca<sup>2+</sup>, with an <italic>A</italic> of 1 being equal to 100% binding capability. The CaM N-lobe EF hands are represented in the left four columns, and the C-lobe EF hands are represented in the right four columns. A rate constant of 1000 s<sup>&#8211;1</sup> represents a rate that was too fast to measure.</p>
###xml 7 689 7 689 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><p textid="29"><bold>Ca<sup>2+</sup> dissociation kinetics of CaM and mutant CaMs</bold></p><p textid="30">The mean dissociation rate constants (<italic>k</italic><sub>off</sub>) and the standard deviation are shown for each EF hand in wild type CaM, CaM12, and CaM34, respectively; <italic>n</italic> refers to the number of independent experiments from which the data was obtained. The relative amplitude (<italic>A</italic>) is also shown for each EF hand; this represents the involvement of the particular hand in the binding of Ca<sup>2+</sup>, with an <italic>A</italic> of 1 being equal to 100% binding capability. The CaM N-lobe EF hands are represented in the left four columns, and the C-lobe EF hands are represented in the right four columns. A rate constant of 1000 s<sup>&#8211;1</sup> represents a rate that was too fast to measure.</p></caption>

###begin p 30
###xml 38 39 38 39 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 39 42 39 42 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
###xml 148 149 148 149 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 256 257 256 257 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 366 368 366 368 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 378 379 378 379 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 583 585 583 585 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
The mean dissociation rate constants (koff) and the standard deviation are shown for each EF hand in wild type CaM, CaM12, and CaM34, respectively; n refers to the number of independent experiments from which the data was obtained. The relative amplitude (A) is also shown for each EF hand; this represents the involvement of the particular hand in the binding of Ca2+, with an A of 1 being equal to 100% binding capability. The CaM N-lobe EF hands are represented in the left four columns, and the C-lobe EF hands are represented in the right four columns. A rate constant of 1000 s-1 represents a rate that was too fast to measure.
###end p 30
###begin p 31
Note that the denotations given to the EF hands are for reference purposes only and do not correlate to the actual hand involved in the reaction.

###begin title 40
RESULTS
###end title 40
###begin title 41
###xml 36 38 36 38 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
Measurement and Interpretation of Ca2+ Dissociation Kinetics of CaM and Its Target Complexes
###end title 41
###begin p 42
###xml 78 80 78 80 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 92 94 92 94 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 125 127 125 127 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 165 167 165 167 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 271 273 271 273 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 316 318 316 318 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 423 425 423 425 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 511 513 511 513 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 730 732 730 732 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 759 760 759 760 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>
###xml 762 763 762 763 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">3</xref>
###xml 765 766 765 766 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">4</xref>
###xml 918 920 914 916 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1069 1071 1057 1059 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1301 1303 1285 1287 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1451 1453 1423 1425 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 1455 1457 1427 1429 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref27">27</xref>
The interaction of CaM with Cx32 N-terminal and C-terminal tail peptides is Ca2+-dependent (12); thus it was expected that Ca2+ dissociation rate constants of CaM Ca2+-binding sites were affected by peptide target binding. The fluorescence intensity of the fluorescent Ca2+ chelator compound quin 2 increases upon Ca2+ binding, and the rate of the quin 2 fluorescence intensity increase is limited by the dissociation of Ca2+ ions from CaM or its peptide complexes. Quin 2 is used in a large excess rendering Ca2+ rebinding to CaM insignificant and thus allowing the observed rates to be interpreted as the rate constants of dissociation. The amplitude of the quin 2 fluorescence increase, which corresponds to the increase in [Ca2+.quin 2], as seen in Figs. 2, 3, 4, is converted to relative fluorescence (RF). The time courses of the change in RF (DeltaRF) are fitted to exponentials to give the rate constants of Ca2+ dissociation. DeltaRF provides a measure of the binding sites involved in each reaction, in our conditions, a DeltaRF of 0.04 corresponded to one Ca2+-binding site. This value was obtained using the data from the experiments with CaM, which showed only two measurable binding sites with a DeltaRF of 0.08; these binding sites correspond to the two sites on the C-terminal lobe. Ca2+ dissociation from the two sites in the N-terminal lobe are too fast to measure by stopped flow kinetics and are estimated to be approximately1000 s-1 (27).
###end p 42
###begin title 43
Secondary Structure Analysis of CaM Mutants
###end title 43
###begin p 44
###xml 288 289 288 289 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 689 691 663 665 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 799 801 773 775 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
CaM and mutant CaMs were characterized by CD spectroscopy to assess the effect of the single-point mutations on the structural integrity of the protein. Two mutant preparations were measured; the means and S.D. of the measurements were as follows: in the apo form, in the presence of 10 mm EGTA, the alpha-helix content of wild type CaM was 46.4 +/- 0.1%. In CaM12, this was reduced to 37.3 +/- 0.1%, and the beta-sheet content decreased from 17.9 +/- 0.1% for wild type to 16.5 +/- 0.1% in CaM12. For CaM34, the alpha-helix content was reduced to 36.5 +/- 0.1%, whereas the beta-sheet content was increased to 29.6 +/- 0.1%. These data show that the single point mutations that disable Ca2+ binding in the EF hands of one CaM lobe resulted in some structural differences in the mutated lobe. The Ca2+ dissociation kinetic experiments presented below were carried out to see whether the functionality of the unmutated lobe was affected.
###end p 44
###begin title 45
###xml 20 22 20 22 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
Comparison of the Ca2+ Dissociation Kinetics of Wild Type and Mutant CaMs
###end title 45
###begin p 46
###xml 95 97 95 97 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 287 293 287 293 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2</xref>
###xml 327 329 323 325 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 353 359 349 355 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2</xref>
###xml 361 369 357 365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">record 1</italic>
###xml 428 429 424 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 422 429 418 425 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 429 439 425 435 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 2</italic>
###xml 458 459 454 455 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 452 459 448 455 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig2" ref-type="fig">Fig. 2<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 459 469 455 465 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 2</italic>
###xml 526 527 522 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 527 530 523 526 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
###xml 564 566 558 560 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 568 569 562 563 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 619 621 611 613 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 623 624 615 616 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 693 695 685 687 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 744 745 736 737 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 745 748 737 740 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
###xml 766 768 756 758 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 770 771 760 761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1033 1035 1023 1025 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1073 1075 1063 1065 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref27">27</xref>
###xml 1095 1102 1085 1092 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
Before using the CaM mutants to determine lobe-specific interactions with Cx32 peptides, the Ca2+ dissociation kinetics of CaM12 and CaM34 were first characterized to see whether the mutations of the EF hands of one lobe affected the functionality of the EF hands of the unmutated lobe. Fig. 2 shows the DeltaRF of quin 2 on Ca2+ dissociation from CaM (Fig. 2, record 1) in comparison with that of our two mutants, CaM12 (Fig. 2A, record 2) and CaM34 (Fig. 2B, record 2), respectively. The average dissociation rate constant (koff) for CaM12 of 11.2 +/- S.D. 0.7 s-1 (n = 4) was similar to that of CaM at 10.9 +/- 1.1 s-1 (n = 4). In contrast, although dissociation from the N-terminal lobe Ca2+-binding sites of CaM was too fast to measure, a koff of 190.4 +/- 15 s-1 (n = 3) was measured for one of the N-terminal lobe EF hands of CaM34, whereas dissociation remained too fast to measure from the other. These data support the understanding that the C-terminal EF hands (binding sites 3 and 4) have a higher affinity for binding Ca2+ than the EF hands of the N-terminal (27). As summarized in Table 1, when the average of all data obtained for each of the CaM mutants is compared against the control CaM data, it is apparent that CaM12 and CaM34 EF hands have largely preserved the functional integrity of CaM.
###end p 46
###begin title 47
###xml 14 16 14 16 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
Kinetics of Ca2+ Dissociation of CaM Complexes with Cx32-derived Peptides
###end title 47
###begin p 48
###xml 0 23 0 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N-terminal Cx32 Peptide</italic>
###xml 108 110 108 110 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 139 140 139 140 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 140 143 140 143 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
###xml 361 363 361 363 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 799 800 799 800 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 805 806 805 806 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 791 806 791 806 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3 (<italic>A</italic> and <italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 830 837 830 837 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">Table 2</xref>
N-terminal Cx32 Peptide-To assess the mechanisms of CaM binding to Cx32-derived peptides, we examined the Ca2+ dissociation rate constant (koff) values of wild type CaM (CaM) and CaM mutants (CaM12 and CaM34) and their complexes with Cx32-derived peptides by stopped flow kinetics. Previously, we have shown that Cx32 1-21 peptide binds CaM with high affinity (12). Here, two homologous peptides, representing the N-terminal tail CaM-binding domain, were examined to determine the mechanism of their interaction with CaM in a lobe-specific manner. Two sequences, corresponding to residues 1-19 and 1-22, were studied to further probe the boundaries of the Cx32 N-terminal tail CaM-binding domain. The kinetic parameters for CaM complexes with Cx32NT peptides 1-19 and Cx32 1-22 are shown in Fig. 3 (A and B, respectively), and in Table 2.
###end p 48
###begin p 49
###xml 30 32 26 28 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 92 93 88 89 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 86 93 82 89 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 93 103 89 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 2</italic>
###xml 173 174 169 170 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 167 174 163 170 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 174 184 170 180 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 1</italic>
###xml 244 246 240 242 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 301 303 295 297 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 305 306 299 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 382 383 376 377 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 383 386 377 380 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">3,4</sub>
###xml 433 435 425 427 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 437 438 429 430 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 520 521 512 513 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 521 522 513 514 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">1</sub>
###xml 647 649 639 641 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 770 772 758 760 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 807 808 795 796 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 801 808 789 796 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 808 818 796 806 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 2</italic>
###xml 895 897 883 885 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1082 1084 1068 1070 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 1086 1087 1072 1073 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1155 1157 1139 1141 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 1159 1160 1143 1144 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 1167 1174 1151 1158 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 1213 1215 1197 1199 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
The amplitude of DeltaRF on Ca2+ dissociation from the CaM.Cx32 1-19 peptide complex (Fig. 3A, record 2) was 1.5-fold greater than that in the absence of the peptide (Fig. 3A, record 1), indicating that the binding of Cx32 1-19 engaged three Ca2+-binding sites, a slower rate constant of 5.1 +/- 1.3 s-1 (n = 3) representing two sites presumed to correspond to the C-lobe EF hands (k3,4), and a faster rate constant of 56.9 +/- 2.3 s-1 (n = 3), thought to correspond to the arbitrarily assigned EF1 of the N-lobe sites (k1). Both represented a marked rate constant reduction compared with those of CaM in the absence of peptide, consistent with Ca2+-dependent peptide binding. A further increase in the DeltaRF value from 0.12 to 0.16 was seen for the dissociation of Ca2+ from CaM.Cx32 1-22 complex (Fig. 3B, record 2) compared with that from the CaM.Cx32 1-19 complex, showing that all four Ca2+-binding sites of CaM were involved in the CaM.Cx32 1-22 peptide complex; the two N-lobe EF hands were involved in the binding of the 1-22 peptide with a rate constant of 10.8 +/- 2.5 s-1 (n = 3) and the CaM C-lobe with a lower rate constant of 1.7 +/- 0.5 s-1 (n = 3) (Table 2). Thus, all four CaM EF hands bound Ca2+ with a higher affinity in the 1-22 complex than when associated with the Cx32 1-19 peptide.
###end p 49

###begin p 52
###xml 83 85 83 85 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 147 148 147 148 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 141 148 141 148 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 148 158 148 158 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 2</italic>
###xml 243 245 241 243 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 247 248 245 246 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 299 301 295 297 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 303 304 299 300 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 329 330 325 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 330 333 326 329 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
###xml 374 375 370 371 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 368 375 364 371 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 375 385 371 381 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 1</italic>
###xml 402 404 396 398 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 410 411 404 405 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 411 414 405 408 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
###xml 516 517 510 511 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">1</xref>
###xml 522 523 516 517 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">2</xref>
###xml 585 586 579 580 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 579 586 573 580 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>D</italic></xref>
###xml 586 596 580 590 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 2</italic>
###xml 612 614 606 608 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 675 677 667 669 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 679 680 671 672 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 724 726 714 716 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 728 729 718 719 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 784 786 774 776 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 876 878 866 868 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 1030 1032 1020 1022 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
When studying the interactions specific to the CaM C-lobe with the CaM12 mutant, Ca2+ dissociation from the CaM12.Cx32 1-19 peptide complex (Fig. 3C, record 2) was biphasic, with one EF hand showing a slow rate of dissociation at 4.9 +/- 0.5 s-1 (n = 3) and the other a faster rate at 18.6 +/- 2.9 s-1 (n = 3). Compared with the koff values for CaM12 without peptide (Fig. 3C, record 1), 11.2 +/- 0.7 s-1, the koff values of CaM12 with the peptide have thus doubled and halved for each EF hand, respectively (Tables 1 and 2), Similarly, when CaM12 was in complex with Cx32 1-22 (Fig. 3D, record 2), a biphasic Ca2+ dissociation occurred, with a rate constant of 3.4 +/- 1.7 s-1 (n = 2) from EF4 and a value of 10.5 +/- 1.3 s-1 (n = 2) from EF3. Thus, although there was evidence of Ca2+-dependent peptide binding to the CaM C-lobe only, cooperativity between the two C-lobe Ca2+-binding sites, seen in CaM, was reduced or lost in the interaction of the Cx32 1-19 or the 1-22 peptide with the CaM C-lobe in the absence of N-lobe Ca2+ binding.
###end p 52
###begin p 53
###xml 123 124 123 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">k</italic>
###xml 124 127 124 127 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">off</sub>
###xml 151 153 149 151 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 155 156 153 154 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 169 170 167 168 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E</italic>
###xml 163 170 161 168 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig3" ref-type="fig">Fig. 3<italic>E</italic></xref>
###xml 170 180 168 178 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 2</italic>
###xml 294 296 290 292 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 314 316 308 310 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 318 319 312 313 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 422 424 416 418 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
In the interaction of the CaM N-lobe with Cx32 1-22, studied by CaM34, both binding sites became involved: EF1 exhibited a koff value of 13.2 +/- 0.2 s-1 (n = 2) (Fig. 3E, record 2), similar to that for EF1 in CaM.Cx32 1-22 complex, whereas the rate constant for EF2 decreased from 190 +/- 15 s-1 to 97.2 +/- 0.5 s-1 (n = 2). These data showed that both peptides could bind to the N-lobe of CaM in the absence of C-lobe Ca2+ binding but substantially more weakly than to CaM. The approximately0.5 binding site fitted to the data may indicate partial engagement of one of the EF hands in the peptide binding.
###end p 53

###xml 490 491 490 491 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 484 491 484 491 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 491 501 491 501 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 2</italic>
###xml 520 522 518 520 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 524 525 522 523 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 625 627 623 625 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 817 818 814 815 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 826 827 823 824 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 820 827 817 824 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 827 837 824 834 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 3</italic>
###xml 856 858 853 855 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 911 912 907 908 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 1092 1094 1084 1086 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref25">25</xref>
C-terminal Cx32 Peptides-Previously, we have shown that the Cx32 C-terminal tail 216-230 peptide binds CaM in a Ca2+-dependent manner but more weakly than the N-terminal tail peptide (12). Here, we investigated whether the Cx32 C-terminal tail CaM-binding domain extends further at the N-terminal end by including residues 208-215. Two peptides were studied: 208-226 and the terminally blocked Ac-208-227-NH2. The rate constant of Ca2+ dissociation from the CaM.Cx32 208-226 complex (Fig. 4A, record 2) was 6.0 +/- 0.9 s-1 (n = 3), reduced from that of unbound CaM, indicating peptide binding to the C-lobe of CaM; the two Ca2+ sites of the N-lobe, however, remained too fast to measure by stopped flow kinetics, indicating that they were not involved in peptide binding. Increasing the peptide concentration to 20 mum (Fig. 4A, record 3) recruited more Ca2+-binding sites compared with that of 208-226 at 10 mum as shown by the greater DeltaRF. An interpretation is that the increase in peptide concentration could have resulted in multiple peptides binding to CaM, as previously suggested (25).
###end p 56
###begin p 57
###xml 22 24 22 24 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 106 108 104 106 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 110 111 108 109 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 124 125 122 123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 118 125 116 123 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 125 135 123 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 4</italic>
###xml 582 589 580 587 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 624 626 620 622 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 628 629 624 625 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 642 643 638 639 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 636 643 632 639 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4<italic>C</italic></xref>
###xml 643 653 639 649 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 3</italic>
###xml 793 795 787 789 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 797 798 791 792 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
The dissociation of Ca2+ from the CaM Cx32 208-227 complex occurred with a rate constant of 13.4 +/- 0.4 s-1 (n = 2) (Fig. 4A, record 4) for one of the N-lobe EF hands; this, however, was only representing involvement of 50% of the EF hand binding. Dissociation from the other N-lobe EF hand remained too fast to measure, indicating that the N-lobe, much like in the case of the Cx32 208-226 peptide, had very little interaction with the peptide. This was corroborated by data on the CaM34 complex with Cx32 208-227; dissociation from one of the EF hands, arbitrarily assigned EF1 (Table 1), was slowed down to 6.3 +/- 0.7 s-1 (n = 2) (Fig. 4C, record 3) and again only seemed to commit half of its binding potential; the dissociation rate from the second site assigned EF2 was 173.1 +/- 0.4 s-1 (n = 2), little affected by the peptide.
###end p 57
###begin p 58
###xml 2 4 2 4 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 91 93 89 91 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 95 96 93 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 109 110 107 108 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 103 110 101 108 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 110 120 108 118 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 4</italic>
###xml 234 236 230 232 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">&#8211;1</sup>
###xml 238 239 234 235 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 286 287 282 283 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 280 287 276 283 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig4" ref-type="fig">Fig. 4<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 287 297 283 293 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 3</italic>
Ca2+ dissociation rates for the C-lobe EF hands were reduced substantially to 2.6 +/- 0.1 s-1 (n = 2) (Fig. 4A, record 4), indicating a strong affinity of the CaM C-lobe for the Cx32 208-227 peptide. The rate constant of 3.1 +/- 0.1 s-1 (n = 1) for both C-lobe EF hands of CaM12 (Fig. 4B, record 3), similar to those for CaM with Cx32 208-227, was consistent with high affinity binding between the CaM C-lobe and the Cx32 C-terminal tail CaM-binding domain. These data showed that CaM binding the Cx32 C-terminal tail CaM-binding domain involves one CaM lobe at a time and demonstrated a marked preference for the CaM C-lobe over the N-lobe.
###end p 58
###begin title 59
CaM Conformation in the Peptide Complexes
###end title 59
###begin p 60
###xml 0 23 0 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">N-terminal Cx32 peptide</italic>
###xml 81 83 81 83 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 300 302 300 302 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref25">25</xref>
###xml 356 358 356 358 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref16">16</xref>
###xml 408 410 408 410 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref17">17</xref>
###xml 419 420 419 420 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 413 420 413 420 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig. 5<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 541 547 541 547 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig5" ref-type="fig">Fig. 5</xref>
###xml 749 750 749 750 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 748 750 748 750 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 815 816 812 813 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 818 819 815 816 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 855 856 852 853 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 923 925 920 922 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">75</sub>
###xml 960 962 957 959 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 964 966 961 963 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref25">25</xref>
N-terminal Cx32 peptide-The Forster resonance energy transfer probe DA-CaM (Ref. 17 and see "Materials and Methods") was used to explore the conformation of CaM in the Cx32 peptide complexes as explained under "Materials and Methods." The smooth muscle myosin light chain kinase-derived Trp peptide (25) with a known compact structure in complex with CaM (16) induced a 79% quenching of DA-CaM fluorescence (17) (Fig. 5A). The degree of DA-CaM fluorescence donor quenching upon increasing concentrations of the Cx32 1-19 peptide is shown in Fig. 5. Maximal donor quenching was 56%, indicating that CaM conformation remained partially extended in complex with the Cx32 1-19 peptide. A weaker complex was also indicated by the dissociation constant (Kd) of DA-CaM for the Cx32 1-19 peptide, which was 1.14 +/- 0.10 mum (n = 1), higher than the value of 27 nm, previously measured for the related Cx32 1-21 peptide using a Lys75-modified fluorescent CaM, TA-CaM (12, 25). Thus, residues 20-21 form an essential part of the Cx32 N-terminal tail CaM-binding domain.
###end p 60

###begin p 63
###xml 0 24 0 24 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C-terminal Cx32 Peptides</italic>
###xml 165 166 165 166 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 159 166 159 166 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 273 274 273 274 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 267 274 267 274 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 274 284 274 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 2</italic>
###xml 376 378 376 378 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 525 526 525 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 519 526 519 526 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 526 536 526 536 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">, record 3</italic>
###xml 660 661 660 661 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 654 661 654 661 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 663 671 663 671 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">record 4</italic>
###xml 821 822 821 822 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 825 827 825 827 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref25">25</xref>
C-terminal Cx32 Peptides-CaM conformation was assessed by examining the maximum donor quenching of DA-CaM induced by Cx32 208-226 peptide binding. As shown in Fig. 6A, the binding of the Cx32 208-226 peptide to DA-CaM was complex. Donor quenching was maximal at 50% (Fig. 6A, record 2). This was consistent with the binding of peptide to one CaM lobe only as shown above by Ca2+ dissociation kinetic experiments. On increasing the peptide concentration, however, a blue shift was seen in the donor AEDANS fluorescence (Fig. 6A, record 3). This was likely to indicate binding of a second peptide molecule to the second CaM lobe. Interestingly, as seen in Fig. 6A (record 4), Trp peptide, even at a large excess, did not fully compete with Cx32 208-226 for CaM. In the light of the high affinity of Trp peptide for CaM (6 pm) (25) in comparison with the relatively low affinity of the Cx32 208-226 peptide, this indicates an unorthodox binding mode between the Cx32 C-terminal tail region and CaM.
###end p 63

###begin p 65
###xml 0 59 0 59 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Equilibrium binding of Cx32 C-terminal peptide with DA-CaM.</bold>
###xml 59 60 59 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 113 114 113 114 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 186 187 186 187 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 192 193 192 193 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 195 203 195 203 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Record 1</italic>
###xml 210 211 210 211 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 220 228 220 228 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">record 2</italic>
###xml 248 249 247 248 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 274 282 273 281 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">record 3</italic>
###xml 310 311 308 309 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 326 334 324 332 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">record 4</italic>
###xml 352 353 349 350 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 367 368 364 365 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 375 376 372 373 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 463 464 460 461 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 469 470 466 467 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2</sub>
###xml 529 530 520 521 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 528 530 519 521 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 550 551 538 539 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
Equilibrium binding of Cx32 C-terminal peptide with DA-CaM.A, aliquots of Cx32 208-226 peptide are added to 433 nm DA-CaM in assay solution (see "Materials and Methods") containing 0.5 mm CaCl2. Record 1, 433 nm DA-CaM; record 2, addition of 0.9 mum Cx32 208-226 to DA-CaM; record 3, further addition of 4.4 mum Cx32 208-226; record 4, addition of 6 mum Trp peptide. B, 150 nm AEDANS-T34C/T110C-CaM in assay solution (see "Materials and Methods") containing 0.5 mm CaCl2 was titrated at 21 degreesC with Cx32 208-226 peptide. A Kd of 3.45 +/- 1.09 mum was obtained for DA-CaM.
###end p 65
###begin p 66
###xml 283 284 283 284 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">d</sub>
###xml 282 284 282 284 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">K<sub>d</sub></italic>
###xml 304 305 301 302 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 307 308 304 305 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">n</italic>
###xml 321 322 318 319 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 315 322 312 319 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig6" ref-type="fig">Fig. 6<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 375 376 371 372 <sc xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">m</sc>
###xml 441 443 437 439 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
The binding affinity of the peptide to CaM was measured taking advantage of the sensitivity of donor fluorescence in DA-CaM to Cx32 208-226 binding. The donor-only labeled probe, AEDANS-T34C/T110C-CaM showed a 2.5-fold increase in fluorescence on 208-226 peptide binding and gave a Kd of 3.45 +/- 1.09 mum (n = 1) (Fig. 6B), a value consistent with previously measured 2.1 mum for TA-CaM for a related peptide representing residues 216-230 (12). These data indicated that the inclusion of residues 208-215 did not increase the CaM binding affinity of the Cx32 C-terminal tail CaM-binding domain.
###end p 66
###begin title 67
DISCUSSION
###end title 67
###begin p 68
###xml 149 151 149 151 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 255 262 255 262 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">in vivo</italic>
CaM association with two CaM-binding domains of Cx32 was characterized by fluorescence stopped flow and equilibrium measurements and by the use of Ca2+ binding-deficient CaM mutants with the aim to gain an insight into the binding of CaM to gap junctions in vivo.
###end p 68
###begin p 69
###xml 418 420 415 417 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 504 511 501 508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 548 550 545 547 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 579 581 576 578 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 665 667 662 664 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
First, the viability of the CaM mutants was tested. Far UV CD spectroscopy revealed changes in the helical, beta-sheet, and loop contents of the CaM12 and CaM34 mutants compared with CaM. The CD results indicated that the EF hand mutations resulted in some changes in the secondary structures of the mutated lobe of CaM12 and CaM34. The functional integrity of CaM12 was, however, shown by the essentially unchanged Ca2+ dissociation rate constants of the CaM12 compared with those of the C-lobe of CaM (Table 1); this also indicated that C-lobe Ca2+ binding is independent of Ca2+ binding to the N-lobe and that the N-lobe mutations had no significant effect on Ca2+ binding by the C-lobe.
###end p 69
###begin p 70
###xml 93 100 93 100 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 221 223 209 211 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 347 349 335 337 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 424 426 412 414 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 475 477 463 465 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 522 524 510 512 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref28">28</xref>
In contrast, whereas mutation of the EF3 and EF4 hands in CaM34 did not affect the EF1 site (Table 1), a significant (approximately6-fold) rate reduction was seen for EF2 when compared with that in CaM. Higher affinity Ca2+ binding by the N-lobe in the absence of the C-lobe is likely to have unmasked the existence of negative cooperativity in Ca2+ binding exerted on the N-lobe by the C-lobe. Previous work showing that Ca2+ binding by the EF3 and EF4 sites destabilizes Ca2+ binding to EF2 via the 76-80 linker region (28) is consistent with this interpretation.
###end p 70
###begin p 71
###xml 220 222 220 222 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 317 324 317 324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="table" rid="tbl2">Table 2</xref>
###xml 346 348 346 348 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 547 549 547 549 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref13">13</xref>
Subtle differences were seen in the functioning of the EF hands of CaM12 in peptide complexes when compared with wild type CaM. Positive cooperativity was lost between EF3 and EF4, as shown by the heterogeneity of the Ca2+ dissociation rate constants of the N-terminal peptides and C-terminal 208-226 bound to CaM12 (Table 2). Cooperativity of Ca2+ binding between EF3 and EF4 was, however, observed again when CaM12 was bound to the Cx32 C-terminal tail 208-227 peptide. These data demonstrate a high level of adaptability in CaM target binding (13).
###end p 71
###begin p 72
###xml 100 106 100 106 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig. 7</xref>
###xml 116 117 116 117 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 122 123 122 123 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 108 124 108 124 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig. 7 (<italic>A</italic> and <italic>B</italic>)</xref>
###xml 263 264 263 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</italic>
###xml 257 264 257 264 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig. 7<italic>A</italic></xref>
###xml 474 476 474 476 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">2+</sup>
###xml 591 592 591 592 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</italic>
###xml 585 592 585 592 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig. 7<italic>B</italic></xref>
###xml 714 716 714 716 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
###xml 838 840 838 840 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref29">29</xref>
Our data suggest some possible binding modes of CaM to Cx32 gap junctions, which are illustrated in Fig. 7. Fig. 7 (A and B) depicts possible arrangements between the N-terminal tail of Cx32 and CaM. If the CaM-binding domain corresponded to residues 1-19 (Fig. 7A), that would cause a weak, dynamic interaction of the CaM N-lobe with the Cx32 N-terminal tail. In contrast, if the 1-22 region of the Cx32 N-terminal tail were accessible for CaM binding, CaM with all four Ca2+-binding sites engaged in the interaction, would have a firm grip on the Cx32 N-terminal CaM-binding domain (Fig. 7B). Previous data suggest that residues 1-21 would have a similarly high affinity interaction to that of the 1-22 peptide (12). The N-terminal tail CaM-binding domain is essential for the trafficking and assembly of functional Cx32 gap junctions (29), it remains to be determined whether and how CaM binding to this region may play a role in the regulation of pore permeability.
###end p 72
###begin p 73
###xml 8 9 8 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">C</italic>
###xml 14 15 14 15 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">D</italic>
###xml 0 16 0 16 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="fig7" ref-type="fig">Fig. 7 (<italic>C</italic> and <italic>D</italic>)</xref>
###xml 609 611 609 611 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="ref12">12</xref>
Fig. 7 (C and D) illustrates the possible binding modes of CaM to the C-terminal tail domain of Cx32. Our data showed that CaM binds to C-terminal Cx32 tail peptides with one lobe at a time. The Cx32 C-terminal tail 208-227 peptide showed a higher affinity for CaM than the 208-226 peptide. The differing results for 208-227 compared with those for 208-226 can be attributed to the acetylation of the N-terminal of the peptide or the addition of the Pro residue and amidation at the C terminus. Both of these extensions to the peptide help it mimic the real sequence in a connexin molecule. In previous work (12), Cx32 C-terminal tail 216-230 peptide was shown to bind CaM with a higher affinity than the 208-226 peptide. This indicates that residues 208-215 do not form part of the CaM-binding domain, and because the VVYLII motif is highly hydrophobic, these residues most likely form part of a transmembrane domain (M4). The Cx32 C-terminal tail CaM-binding domain therefore best corresponds to residues 216-227, and the CaM binding site is likely to be terminated by the 227-228 Pro-Pro sequence.
###end p 73
###begin p 74
###xml 0 9 0 9 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">FIGURE 7.</label>
